ns-0 ns-subject page-Freediving rootpage-Freediving skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Freediving</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Underwater diving without breathing apparatus</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Junko-Kitahama_Apnea-Monofin_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Junko-Kitahama_Apnea-Monofin_cropped.jpg/220px-Junko-Kitahama_Apnea-Monofin_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Junko-Kitahama_Apnea-Monofin_cropped.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="286" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Junko-Kitahama_Apnea-Monofin_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Freediver with <a href="/wiki/Monofin" title="Monofin">monofin</a>, ascending</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Freediving</b>, <b>free-diving</b>, <b>free diving</b>, <b>breath-hold diving</b>, or <b>skin diving</b> is a form of <a href="/wiki/Underwater_diving" title="Underwater diving">underwater diving</a> that relies on breath-holding until resurfacing rather than the use of breathing apparatus such as <a href="/wiki/Scuba_set" title="Scuba set">scuba gear</a>.\n</p><p>Besides the limits of breath-hold, immersion in water and exposure to high ambient pressure also have physiological effects that limit the depths and duration possible in freediving.\n</p><p>Examples of freediving activities are: <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_fishing" title="Artisanal fishing">traditional fishing</a> techniques, competitive and non-competitive freediving, competitive and non-competitive <a href="/wiki/Spearfishing" title="Spearfishing">spearfishing</a> and freediving <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" class="mw-redirect" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_football" title="Underwater football">underwater football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_rugby" title="Underwater rugby">underwater rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_hockey" title="Underwater hockey">underwater hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_target_shooting" title="Underwater target shooting">underwater target shooting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkeling</a>. There are also a range of "competitive apnea" disciplines; in which competitors attempt to attain great depths, times, or distances on a single breath.\n</p><p>Historically, the term <i>free diving</i> was also used to refer to <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a>, due to the freedom of movement compared with <a href="/wiki/Surface_supplied_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Surface supplied diving">surface supplied diving</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rebikoff_1955_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rebikoff_1955-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Owen_1955_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Owen_1955-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taillez_et_al_1957_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taillez_et_al_1957-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Fiction"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Fiction</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sponge_diving" title="Sponge diving">Sponge diving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pearl_hunting" title="Pearl hunting">Pearl hunting</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sponges.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sponges.JPG/250px-Sponges.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sponges.JPG/375px-Sponges.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sponges.JPG/500px-Sponges.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sponges.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">Natural sponges</a> have been harvested by freedivers near the Greek island of <a href="/wiki/Kalymnos" title="Kalymnos">Kalymnos</a> since at least the time of <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In ancient times freediving without the aid of mechanical devices was the only possibility, with the exception of the occasional use of reeds and leather breathing bladders.<sup id="cite_ref-Desislava_et_al_1999_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Desislava_et_al_1999-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The divers faced the same problems as divers today, such as <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deep_water_blackout" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep water blackout">blacking out</a> during a breath hold. Freediving was practiced in <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">ancient cultures</a> to <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">gather food</a>, harvest resources such as <a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">sponge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pearl" title="Pearl">pearl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_salvage" title="Marine salvage">reclaim sunken valuables</a>, and to help aid <a href="/wiki/Military_campaign" title="Military campaign">military campaigns</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In Ancient Greece, both <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a> mention the <a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">sponge</a> as being used for bathing. The island of <a href="/wiki/Kalymnos" title="Kalymnos">Kalymnos</a> was a main centre of <a href="/wiki/Sponge_diving" title="Sponge diving">diving for sponges</a>. By using weights (<a href="/wiki/Skandalopetra" class="mw-redirect" title="Skandalopetra">skandalopetra</a>) of as much as 15 kilograms (33&#160;lb) to speed the descent, breath-holding divers would descend to depths up to 30 metres (98&#160;ft) to collect sponges.<sup id="cite_ref-Hendrickse_and_Merks_2009_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hendrickse_and_Merks_2009-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Harvesting of <a href="/wiki/Coral_(precious)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral (precious)">red coral</a> was also done by divers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> had large amounts of maritime trade. As a result of <a href="/wiki/Shipwrecks" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipwrecks">shipwrecks</a>, particularly in the fierce winter storms, divers were often hired to salvage whatever they could from the seabed.<sup id="cite_ref-Galili_and_Rosen_2008_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Galili_and_Rosen_2008-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Divers would swim down to the wreck and choose the most valuable pieces to salvage.\n</p><p>Divers were also used in warfare. Defenses against sea vessels were often created, such as underwater <a href="/wiki/Barricade" title="Barricade">barricades</a>, and hence divers were often used to scout out the seabed when ships were approaching an enemy harbor. If barricades were found, it was divers who were used to disassemble them, if possible.<sup id="cite_ref-Frost_1968_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frost_1968-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnesian_War" title="Peloponnesian War">Peloponnesian War</a>, divers were used to get past enemy <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockades</a> to relay messages as well as supplies to allies or troops that were cut off,<sup id="cite_ref-Thucydides_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thucydides-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and in 332 BC, during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tyre_(332_BC)" title="Siege of Tyre (332 BC)">Siege of Tyre</a>, the city used divers to cut the anchor cables of <a href="/wiki/Alexander" title="Alexander">Alexander</a>\'s attacking ships.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In Japan, <a href="/wiki/Ama_divers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ama divers"><i>ama</i> divers</a> began to collect pearls about 2,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-uhms1985_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uhms1985-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ama_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ama-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\nFor thousands of years, most seawater pearls were retrieved by divers working in the Indian Ocean, in areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mannar" title="Gulf of Mannar">Gulf of Mannar</a> (between <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-De_Silva_1995_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Silva_1995-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A fragment of <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Charax" title="Isidore of Charax">Isidore of Charax</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthian</a> itinerary was preserved in <a href="/wiki/Athenaeus" title="Athenaeus">Athenaeus</a>\'s 3rd-century <i><a href="/wiki/Sophists_at_Dinner" class="mw-redirect" title="Sophists at Dinner">Sophists at Dinner</a></i>, recording freediving for pearls around an island in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Isidore_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isidore-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pearl divers near the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> were also successful at harvesting large pearls, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Archipelago" title="Sulu Archipelago">Sulu Archipelago</a>.  At times, the largest pearls belonged by law to the sultan, and selling them could result in the death penalty for the seller.  Nonetheless, many pearls made it out of the archipelago by stealth, ending up in the possession of the wealthiest families in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Sooloo_archipelago_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sooloo_archipelago-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Pearling was popular in Qatar, Bahrain, Japan, and India. The Gulf of Mexico was also known for pearling.\n<a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a> harvested freshwater pearls from lakes and rivers like the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_River" title="Tennessee River">Tennessee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>, while others dived for marine pearls from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and waters along the coasts of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.\n</p><p>In 1940, Dottie Frazier pioneered freediving for women and also began teaching classes. It was also during this time that she began to design and sell rubber suits for Navy UDT divers.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Freediving_activities">Freediving activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Freediving activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational_hunting_and_gathering">Recreational hunting and gathering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recreational hunting and gathering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spearfishing">Spearfishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spearfishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Spearfishing" title="Spearfishing">Spearfishing</a> is an ancient method of <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> that has been used throughout the world for millennia. Early civilizations were familiar with the custom of spearing fish from rivers and streams using sharpened sticks.\n</p><p>Today modern spearfishing makes use of elastic powered <a href="/wiki/Speargun" title="Speargun">spearguns</a> and slings, or compressed gas pneumatic powered spearguns, to strike the hunted fish. Specialised techniques and equipment have been developed for various types of aquatic environments and target fish. Spearfishing may be done using <a href="/wiki/Free-diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-diving">free-diving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snorkelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Snorkelling">snorkelling</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> techniques. Spearfishing while using scuba equipment is illegal in some countries. The use of mechanically powered spearguns is also outlawed in some countries and jurisdictions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Spearfishing is highly selective, normally uses no bait and has no <a href="/wiki/By-catch" class="mw-redirect" title="By-catch">by-catch</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collection_of_shellfish">Collection of shellfish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Collection of shellfish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_breath-hold_watersports">Competitive breath-hold watersports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Competitive breath-hold watersports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aquathlon">Aquathlon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Aquathlon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Aquathlon (also known as underwater wrestling) is an underwater sport where two competitors wearing masks and fins wrestle underwater in an attempt to remove a ribbon from each other\'s ankle band in order to win the bout. The "combat" takes place in a 5-metre (16&#160;ft) square ring within a swimming pool, and is made up of three 30-second rounds, with a fourth round played in the event of a tie. The sport originated during the 1980s in the former USSR (now Russia) and was first played at international level in 1993. It was recognised by the Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques (CMAS) in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Aquathlon_History_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aquathlon_History-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aquathlon_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aquathlon-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ceduno_2009_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ceduno_2009-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CMAS_Aquathlon_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS_Aquathlon-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_spearfishing">Competitive spearfishing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Competitive spearfishing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Competitive spearfishing is defined by the world governing body <a href="/wiki/World_Underwater_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Underwater Federation">CMAS</a> as "the hunting and capture of fish underwater without the aid of artificial breathing devices, using gear that depends entirely on the physical strength of the competitor." They publish a set of competition rules that are used by affiliated organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-CMAS_Spearfishing_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS_Spearfishing-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spearfishing_rules_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spearfishing_rules-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synchronised_swimming">Synchronised swimming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Synchronised swimming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg/170px-Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg/255px-Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg/340px-Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1703" data-file-height="2555" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Open_Make_Up_For_Ever_2013_-_Team_-_Japan_-_10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A member of the Japanese team is thrown up in the air by other members under the water during the team\'s free routine at the 2013 French Open.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" class="mw-redirect" title="Synchronized swimming">Synchronized swimming</a> is a hybrid form of <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance" title="Dance">dance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a>,  consisting of swimmers (either solos, duets, trios, combos, or teams) performing a synchronised routine of elaborate moves in the water, accompanied by music. Synchronised swimming demands advanced water skills, and requires great strength, endurance, flexibility, grace, artistry and precise timing, as well as exceptional breath control when upside down underwater. During lifts swimmers are not allowed to touch the bottom.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Traditionally it was a women\'s sport, but following the addition of a new mixed-pair event, <a href="/wiki/FINA_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="FINA World Aquatics Championships">FINA World Aquatics competitions</a> are open to men since <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="2015 World Aquatics Championships">the 16th 2015 championships in Kazan</a>, and the other international and national competitions allow male competitors in every event. However, men are currently still barred from competing in the Olympics. Both <a href="/w/index.php?title=USA_Synchro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="USA Synchro (page does not exist)">USA Synchro</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Synchro_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Synchro Canada (page does not exist)">Synchro Canada</a> allow men to compete with women. Most European countries also allow men to compete, and France even allows male only podiums, according to the number of participants. In the past decade more men are becoming involved in the sport and a global biannual competition called <a href="/wiki/Men%27s_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Men&#39;s Cup">Men\'s Cup</a> has been steadily growing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Swimmers perform two routines for the judges, one technical and one free, as well as age group routines and figures. Synchronised swimming is both an individual and team sport.  Swimmers compete individually during figures, and then as a team during the routine.  Figures are made up of a combination of skills and positions that often require control, strength, and flexibility.  Swimmers are ranked individually for this part of the competition.  The routine involves teamwork and synchronization.  It is choreographed to music and often has a theme. Synchronised swimming is governed internationally by <a href="/wiki/FINA" title="FINA">FINA</a> (F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Internationale de Natation).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Underwater_hockey">Underwater hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Underwater hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG/220px-OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG/330px-OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG/440px-OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OctopushTwoPlayers28092009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two players compete for the puck in underwater hockey</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Underwater_Hockey" class="mw-redirect" title="Underwater Hockey">Underwater Hockey</a>, (also called <b>Octopush</b> (mainly in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>)) is a globally played limited-<a href="/wiki/Contact_sport" title="Contact sport">contact sport</a> in which two teams compete to manoeuvre a <a href="/wiki/Hockey_puck" title="Hockey puck">puck</a> across the bottom of a <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">swimming pool</a> into the opposing team\'s <a href="/wiki/Goal_(sport)" title="Goal (sport)">goal</a> by propelling it with a <a href="/wiki/Hockey_stick" title="Hockey stick">pusher</a>.  It originated in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> in 1954 when Alan Blake, the founder of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Southsea" title="Southsea">Southsea</a> Sub-Aqua Club, invented the game he called Octopush as a means of keeping the club\'s members interested and active over the cold winter months when open-water diving lost its appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-CMAS_Hockey_history_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS_Hockey_history-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Underwater Hockey is now played worldwide, with the <a href="/wiki/Conf%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Mondiale_des_Activit%C3%A9s_Subaquatiques" title="Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques">Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques</a>, abbreviated CMAS, as the world governing body.<sup id="cite_ref-CMAS_Hockey_comission_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS_Hockey_comission-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Underwater_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Underwater Hockey World Championships">Underwater Hockey World Championship</a> was held in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> in 1980 after a false start in 1979 brought about by international politics and apartheid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Underwater_football">Underwater football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Underwater football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg/220px-US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg/330px-US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg/440px-US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_110603-N-AD372-308_Students_at_the_Naval_Diving_and_Salvage_Training_Center_play_underwater_football_to_cool_down_after_physical_training.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US Navy Students playing underwater football</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Underwater_football" title="Underwater football">Underwater football</a> is a two-team <a href="/wiki/Underwater_sports" title="Underwater sports">underwater sport</a> that shares common elements with <a href="/wiki/Underwater_hockey" title="Underwater hockey">underwater hockey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Underwater_rugby" title="Underwater rugby">underwater rugby</a>. As with both of those games, it is played in a <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">swimming pool</a> with <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkeling</a> equipment (<a href="/wiki/Diving_mask" title="Diving mask">mask</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swimfins" class="mw-redirect" title="Swimfins">fins</a>). The goal of the game is to <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/manoeuvre" class="extiw" title="wikt:manoeuvre">manoeuvre</a> (by <a href="/wiki/Carry_(American_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carry (American football)">carrying</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forward_pass" title="Forward pass">passing</a>) a slightly <a href="/wiki/Buoyancy" title="Buoyancy">negatively buoyant</a> <a href="/wiki/Ball" title="Ball">ball</a> from one side of a pool to the other by players who are completely submerged <a href="/wiki/Underwater" title="Underwater">underwater</a>. <a href="/wiki/Score_(sport)" title="Score (sport)">Scoring</a> is achieved by placing the ball (under control) in the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gutter" class="extiw" title="wikt:gutter">gutter</a> on the side of the pool. Variations include using a toy rubber torpedo as the ball, and weighing down buckets to rest on the bottom and serve as goals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>It is played in the Canadian provinces of <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-where_played_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-where_played-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Underwater_rugby">Underwater rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Underwater rugby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Underwater_rugby" title="Underwater rugby">Underwater rugby</a> is an underwater team sport. During a match two teams try to score a negatively buoyant ball (filled with saltwater) into the opponents\xe2\x80\x99 goal at the bottom of a swimming pool. It originated from within the physical fitness training regime existing in German diving clubs during the early 1960s and has little in common with rugby football except for the name. It was recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Conf%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Mondiale_des_Activit%C3%A9s_Subaquatiques" title="Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques">Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques</a> (CMAS) in 1978 and was first played as a world championship in 1980.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Underwater_target_shooting">Underwater target shooting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Underwater target shooting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Underwater_target_shooting" title="Underwater target shooting">Underwater target shooting</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Underwater_sports" title="Underwater sports">underwater sport</a> that tests a competitors\xe2\x80\x99 ability to accurately use a <a href="/wiki/Speargun" title="Speargun">speargun</a> via a set of individual and team events conducted in a <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">swimming pool</a> using <a href="/wiki/Free_diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Free diving">free diving</a> or Apnea technique.  The sport was developed in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> during the early 1980s and is currently practised mainly in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.  It is known as <i>Tir sur cible subaquatique</i> in French and as <i>Tiro al Blanco Subacu\xc3\xa1tico</i> in Spanish.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_apnea">Competitive apnea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Competitive apnea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg/220px-Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg/330px-Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg/440px-Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Freediver-monofin-start-london-competition-2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monofin freediver</div></div></div>\n<p>Competitive freediving is currently governed by two world associations: <a href="/wiki/AIDA_International" title="AIDA International">AIDA International</a> (International Association for Development of Apnea)<sup id="cite_ref-RRR8947_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RRR8947-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Conf%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Mondiale_des_Activit%C3%A9s_Subaquatiques" title="Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques">CMAS</a> (Conf\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration Mondiale des Activit\xc3\xa9s Subaquatiques \xe2\x80\x93 World Underwater Federation). Historically, there were two more organisations that regulated freediving records and activities - <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Association_of_Freedivers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Association of Freedivers (page does not exist)">IAFD</a> (International Association of Freedivers) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving_Regulations_and_Education_Entity&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Freediving Regulations and Education Entity (page does not exist)">FREE</a> (Freediving Regulations and Education Entity).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Each organization has its own rules on recognizing a record attempt which can be found on the organization\'s website. Alongside <i>competitive disciplines</i> there are <i>record disciplines</i> - disciplines that are not held in competitions, that are just for setting world records. There is a third organization which in addition to AIDA and CMAS preside over those record disciplines and that is Guinness.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Almost all types of competitive freediving have in common that it is an individual sport based on the best individual achievement. Exceptions to this rule are the bi-annual World Championship for Teams held by AIDA, where the combined score of the team members makes up the team\'s total points and <a href="/wiki/Skandalopetra_diving" title="Skandalopetra diving">Skandalopetra diving</a> competitions held by CMAS, the only truly \xe2\x80\x98team\xe2\x80\x99 event in freediving - for which teams are formed by two athletes: one acting as an apneista (Voutichtis; diver) and the other acting as an assistant (Kolaouzeris; person who "extracts").\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disciplines">Disciplines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Disciplines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are currently eleven recognized disciplines defined by AIDA and CMAS, and a dozen more that are only practiced locally.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="what are the dozen more? (December 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> All disciplines can be practiced by both men and women and only CMAS currently separates records in fresh water from those at sea. The disciplines of AIDA can be done both in competition and as a record attempt, with the exception of Variable Weight and No limits, which are both solely for record attempts. For all AIDA depth disciplines, the depth the athlete will attempt is announced before the dive; this is accepted practice for both competition and record attempts. Most divers choose monofin over bifins where there is a choice.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Discipline\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Measure&#173;ment\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">AIDA<sup id="cite_ref-AIDA-disciplines_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIDA-disciplines-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">CMAS<sup id="cite_ref-CMAS-disciplines_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMAS-disciplines-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th class="unsortable" rowspan="2">Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>open water\n</th>\n<th>pool\n</th>\n<th>open water\n</th>\n<th>pool\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left" bgcolor="#f2f2f2"><b>CWT</b> \xe2\x80\x93 <b><a href="/wiki/Constant_weight_apnea" title="Constant weight apnea">Constant&#160;weight&#160;apnea</a></b></td>\n<td>depth</td>\n<td><img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td><img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span></td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="left">Maximum depth following a guide line. class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Note 1: Best official result in STA is Guinness WR of 11:54 by Branko Petrovi\xc4\x87 in 2014, a freediver who has results in STA over 10 minutes under both AIDA and CMAS.</i>\n<br /><i>Note 2: Best NLT result is 253.2m by Herbert Nitsch in 2012; intention of having the dive sanctioned by AIDA fell through due to a sponsoring src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg/220px-Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg/330px-Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg/440px-Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mohamed_Adel_Recreational_freediving.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Recreational freediving in Dahab</div></div></div>\n<p>Freediving as a recreational activity is widely practiced and differs significantly from <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a>. Although there are potential risks to all freediving, it can be safely practiced using a wide range of skill levels from the average snorkeler to the professional freediver. Compared to scuba diving, freediving offers:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> \n</p>\n<ul><li>Freedom from cumbersome equipment and short preparation times.</li>\n<li>Low cost.</li>\n<li>It is quiet and does not disturb fish, the noise of breathing and bubbles can be quite loud on open circuit scuba though <a href="/wiki/Rebreather" title="Rebreather">rebreathers</a> are much quieter.</li>\n<li>Mobility and speed, but for a much more limited period.</li>\n<li>No decompression time for deep dives, although it is possible to get decompression sickness, or <a href="/wiki/Taravana" title="Taravana">taravana</a>, from repetitive deep free-diving with short surface intervals.<sup id="cite_ref-Wong_1999_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wong_1999-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The lack of exhaled air bubbles on ascent gives greater visibility on ascent.</li>\n<li>Accessibility, if the site can be walked to it can, potentially, be dived.</li>\n<li>Appropriately skilled and fit freedivers can go as deep, or deeper than, recreational scuba divers, the depth being limited only by the willingness to accept the risks; scuba diving is restricted by the level of certification.</li></ul>\n<p>Freshwater springs, often with excellent visibility, provide good freediving opportunities but with greater risks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Diving into spring caverns with restricted access to the surface is very different from diving in open water and requires careful planning and an appropriate level of fitness. The time available to a freediver to solve problems underwater before hypoxia sets in is severely restricted in comparison with scuba.  The following general considerations apply:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Every spring cave is unique and local knowledge needs to be sought for each one.</li>\n<li>The risk of drowning is greatly increased by an overhead environment, lack of light, silting, lack of or loss of a guideline and spatial disorientation.</li>\n<li>A lateral swim to the exit point may be required before being able to ascend.</li>\n<li>If a current is present, the exit route must be planned to go with it.</li>\n<li>A dive light, with at least one backup, will be required for deeper penetrations.</li>\n<li>Stirring up silt will lead to loss of visibility or light.</li>\n<li>Shorter fins are better in confined and silty spaces; a monofin is generally impractical.</li>\n<li>The cave walls or rocks may offer handholds to assist entry and exit.</li>\n<li>Air pockets found inside the cave are usually unsafe to breathe from.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physiology">Physiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Physiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Physiology_of_underwater_diving" title="Physiology of underwater diving">Physiology of underwater diving</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(July 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The human body has several oxygen-conserving adaptations that manifest under diving conditions as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mammalian_diving_reflex" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammalian diving reflex">mammalian diving reflex</a>. The adaptations include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Reflex_bradycardia" title="Reflex bradycardia">Reflex bradycardia</a>: Significant drop in heart rate.</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blood-shift&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blood-shift (page does not exist)">Blood-shift</a>: Blood flow and volume is redistributed towards vital organs by means of a reflex vasoconstriction. Blood vessels distend and become engorged, which in the case of the pulmonary capillaries assists with pressure compensation that comes with increasing diving depth, and without which a largely air-filled chest cavity would simply collapse for lack of compliance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>Body-cooling: peripheral <a href="/wiki/Vasoconstriction" title="Vasoconstriction">vasoconstriction</a> results in cooling of peripheral tissue beds, which lower their oxygen demand in a thermodynamic manner. In addition, Murat et al. (2013) recently discovered that breath-holding results in prompt and substantial brain cooling, just like in diving birds and seals. (Dry) breath-holds result in cooling on the order of about 1&#160;\xc2\xb0C/minute, but this is likely to be greater with cold water submersion, in proportion to the magnitude and promptness of the dive response.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Splenic_contraction&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Splenic contraction (page does not exist)">Splenic contraction</a>: Releasing red blood cells carrying oxygen.<sup id="cite_ref-Milton_2004_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milton_2004-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Techniques">Techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Breath-holding ability, and hence dive performance, is a function of on-board oxygen stores, scope for metabolic rate reduction, efficient oxygen utilization, and hypoxia tolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid22753202_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22753202-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Various athletes attempt to accomplish this in various ways. Most divers rely on increasing fitness by increasing lung capacity. Some use "packing", which increases lung volume beyond normal total lung capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-RRR10026_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RRR10026-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Simple breath-holding practice is highly effective for increasing lung capacity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In addition, training is allocated to enhance blood and muscle oxygen stores, to a limited extent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Training">Training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Training for freediving can take many forms, some of which can be performed on land.\n</p><p>One example is the apnea walk. This consists of a preparation "breathe-up", followed by a short (typically 1 minute) breath hold taken at rest. Without breaking the hold, participants then begin walking as far as possible until it becomes necessary to breathe again. Athletes can do close to 400 meters in training this way.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>This form of training is good for accustoming <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a> to work under <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental)" title="Hypoxia (environmental)">anaerobic</a> conditions, and for tolerance to <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO<sub>2</sub></a> build-up in the circulation. It is also easy to gauge progress, as increasing distance can be measured.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Before competition attempts, freedivers perform a preparation sequence, which usually consists of physical stretching, mental exercise and breath exercise. It may include a succession of variable length static apnea and special purging deep breaths. Results of the preparation sequence are slower metabolism, lower heart rate and breath rate, and lower levels of carbon dioxide in the bloodstream<sup id="cite_ref-aaus1997_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaus1997-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and overall mental equilibrium.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hazards">Hazards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Hazards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b> <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(January 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Risk">Risk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Risk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Freediving_blackout" title="Freediving blackout">Freediving blackout</a></div>\n<p>Failing to respond to physiological warning signals, or crossing the mental barrier by strong will, may lead to <a href="/wiki/Freediving_blackout" title="Freediving blackout">blackout</a> underwater or on reaching the surface.<sup id="cite_ref-uhms1985_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uhms1985-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-danworkshop_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-danworkshop-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Trained freedivers are well aware of this and competitions must be held under strict supervision and with competent first-aiders on standby.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid16602257_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16602257-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, this does not eliminate the risk of blackout. Freedivers are encouraged to dive only with a \'buddy\' who accompanies them, observing from in the water at the surface, and ready to dive to the rescue if the diver loses consciousness during the ascent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Due to the nature of the sport, any practice of freediving must include strict adherence to safety measures as an integral part of the activity, and all participants must also be adept in rescue and resuscitation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Without proper training and supervision, competitive freediving/apnea/breath-hold diving is extremely dangerous.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_and_notable_accidents">Statistics and notable accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Statistics and notable accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Mevoli" title="Nicholas Mevoli">Nicholas Mevoli</a>, a diver from New York died on 17 November 2013 after losing consciousness on surfacing from a 3-minute 38 second dive to a depth of 72 metres during an official record attempt in the "constant weight without fins" event. He had previously reached greater depths and longer times in other disciplines.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiction_and_documentaries">Fiction and documentaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Fiction and documentaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(September 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Documentaries">Documentaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Documentaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><i>Ocean Men</i> (2001) is a documentary film about the art and science of freediving, featuring two of its most outstanding exponents: <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Ferreras" title="Francisco Ferreras">Francisco "Pip\xc3\xadn" Ferreras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Pelizzari" title="Umberto Pelizzari">Umberto Pelizzari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiction">Fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Freediving&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>In the film <i><a href="/wiki/Mission_Impossible_-_Rogue_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission Impossible - Rogue Nation">Mission Impossible - Rogue Nation</a></i>, Tom Cruise plays super spy Ethan Hunt fighting the forces of evil, and goes freediving in a scene to expose the villains.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Pearl_(novel)" title="The Pearl (novel)">The Pearl</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Steinbeck" title="John Steinbeck">John Steinbeck</a> (1947) is a novel about a poor pearl diver, Kino, who finds the \'Pearl of Heaven\', which is exceptionally valuable, changing his life forever.  The novel explores themes of man\'s nature as well as greed and evil.</li>\n<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/South_Sea_Adventure" title="South Sea Adventure">South Sea Adventure</a></i> (1952) by <a href="/wiki/Willard_Price" title="Willard Price">Willard Price</a> the Hunt brothers, marooned on a coral island, use free diving to collect both pearls and fresh water.</li>\n<li>In <a href="/wiki/Ian_Fleming" title="Ian Fleming">Ian Fleming\'s</a> (1964) <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(novel)" title="You Only Live Twice (novel)">You Only Live Twice</a></i>, the character <a href="/wiki/Kissy_Suzuki" title="Kissy Suzuki">Kissy Suzuki</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Ama_divers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ama divers">ama diver</a>. This connection was also mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(film)" title="You Only Live Twice (film)">film version</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Man_from_Atlantis" title="Man from Atlantis">Man from Atlantis</a></i> was a 1970s TV series which featured a <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">superhero</a> with the ability to breathe underwater and freedive in his own special way.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Blue" title="The Big Blue">The Big Blue</a></i> (1988) is a romantic film about two world-class freedivers, a heavily fictionalized depiction of the rivalry of freedivers <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Mayol" title="Jacques Mayol">Jacques Mayol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Maiorca" title="Enzo Maiorca">Enzo Maiorca</a>.</li>\n<li>In the movie <i>Phoenix Blue</i> (2001), protagonist Rick is a musician who freedives competitively.</li>\n<li>The children\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dolphins_of_Laurentum" title="The Dolphins of Laurentum">The Dolphins of Laurentum</a></i> by Caroline Lawrence (2003), which takes place in ancient Rome, describes the applications of freediving (sponge and pearl diving) and its hazards, as one of the principal characters, as well as the main antagonist, try to beat each other to a sunken treasure.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Freediver" title="The Freediver">The Freediver</a></i> (2004) is a film about a talented female freediver who is discovered and brought to an island, where she is trained by an ambitious scientist to break a freediving world record currently held by an American woman.</li>\n<li>In the film <i><a href="/wiki/Into_the_Blue_(2005_film)" title="Into the Blue (2005 film)">Into the Blue</a></i> (2005) starring <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Alba" title="Jessica Alba">Jessica Alba</a>, a group of divers find themselves in deep trouble with a drug lord after they come upon the illicit cargo of a sunken airplane in the Caribbean.  Jessica Alba is an accomplished freediver, and did much of the underwater work; some other stunts were performed by <a href="/wiki/Mehgan_Heaney-Grier" title="Mehgan Heaney-Grier">Mehgan Heaney-Grier</a>.</li>\n<li>In <a href="/wiki/Greg_Iles" title="Greg Iles">Greg Iles</a>\' novel <i>Blood Memory</i> (2005), the main character Cat Ferry is an <a href="/wiki/Odontologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Odontologist">odontologist</a> and a freediver.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/H2O:_Just_Add_Water" title="H2O: Just Add Water">H<sub>2</sub>O: Just Add Water</a></i> Series 3 added a freediver (Will Benjamin played by <a href="/wiki/Luke_Mitchell" title="Luke Mitchell">Luke Mitchell</a>) as a regular.  Freediving is featured in some episodes.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Greater_Meaning_of_Water" class="mw-redirect" title="The Greater Meaning of Water">The Greater Meaning of Water</a></i> (2010) is an independent film about competitive constant weight freediving, focusing on the \'zen\' of freediving.</li>\n<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> <a href="/wiki/Television_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Television series">television series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Corner_Gas" title="Corner Gas">Corner Gas</a></i>, the character Karen Pelly (<a href="/wiki/Tara_Spencer-Nairn" title="Tara Spencer-Nairn">Tara Spencer-Nairn</a>) competed in static apnea, ranking fifth in Canada with a personal best of over six minutes.</li>\n<li>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Television_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Television series">television series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i> episode "The Chamber" (Session 2, Episode 17), the character <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Buchannon" title="Mitch Buchannon">Mitch Buchannon</a> rescues a diver trapped 90 feet below the ocean surface, but almost dies while suffering the effects of <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>; decompression sickness is highly improbable following freediving exposure to this depth.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Accessed 13 Aug 2014.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Sooloo_archipelago-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Sooloo_archipelago_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.farlang.com/gemstones/streeter_pearls_and_pearling/page_137">Streeter\'s Pearls and pearling life</a> dedicates a chapter to the Sooloo islands. Streeter was one of the leading and most influential English jewelers in the 19th century and outfitted his own schooner the Shree-Pas-Sair which he sailed as well and on which he himself went pearl fishing in 1880. (For an illustration of divers on a schooner, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.farlang.com/gemstones/streeter_pearls_and_pearling/page_001">Pearl fishers obtaining the world\'s best pearls</a>.
